</style>

<div class="word-content">
<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>III. GENERAL MECHANICS BEHIND INTERPRETATION </span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>Virgil Warren, PhD</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The big three in interpretation are (1)
the law of harmony, (2) the law of contrast, and (3) the nature of the case. All
three amount to one thingthe law of harmony, but we sort them out to stress
the peculiar contribution each aspect makes to the whole.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  A. Law of harmony (analogy)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Two things or two ideas can have
varying degrees and kinds of relationship. From one extreme to the other is (1)
what is positively determined by something else,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   (2) what fits
with something else,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   (3) what is
relevant to something else,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   (4) what is
foreign to something else,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>    (5)
what works against something else,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   (6)
what is incompatible with something else.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>The law of harmony in interpretation deals with the
first three entries in this list.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The law of harmony equals the law
of context; it deals with consistency. It asks who is speaking, who is
addressed, when something is said, where it is said, what the topic is. Consistency
is one test of proper interpretation, although it is a negative test rather
than a positive one. A negative test eliminates some error but does not
guarantee truth. Consistency is a characteristic of truth, but something may be
consistent with known facts without being true. Context relates to the piece of
<u>writing</u> (near and distant context), the <u>historical background</u>,
and the <u>reality</u> discussed. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>Three dots cannot fit with a straight
line, but they could fit with a circle, a triangle, and square, and other
figures.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (a) <u>Near context</u>
(circumstance), which means the immediate subject of discussionwhat the author
is talking about. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>An example of near context comes from
Mark<b> 15</b>:47. In the Greek, the reader cannot tell from the context whether
<i>Mary the ______ of Joses</i> was his mother or his wife except by distant
context in <b>15</b>:40: <i>Mary the mother of James the Less and Joses.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (b) <u>Distant context</u>
(collation) refers to a widening series of surroundings: the rest of the book,
the rest of this authors writings, the rest of the New Testament, the rest of
revelation, the total Christian understanding (what harmonizes with the whole
of scripture; note the expression analogy of scripture). Distant context
brings into view the nature of scripture. If parts of the gospels, for example,
are pieced together from all kinds of sources, the resulting crazy quilt cannot
provide a context for individual pieces. All we can say is that the redactor
saw some connection between the pieces when he put them together as the
scribes may have done when they copied out Solomons proverbs and arranged
them into the book by that name.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (c) <u>Cultural context</u>
means the historical situation at the time of writing, including customs (<i>Sitz
im Leben</i>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (d) <u>The nature of the case</u>
as learned from experience (Note gestalt.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Consistency applies to (a) the
compatibility of ideas and (b) the compatibility of reasoning patterns (by
parity of reason). A principle of interpretation that cannot be applied
consistently should not be applied at all (cp. <i>What the Bible Says About
Salvation</i>, pp. 386-87). Circumstance (context), collation (with other
texts), and application belong together. (See Philosophical and Religious
Dimensions of the American Founding, by Ellis Sandoz in <i>The Intercollegiate
Review </i>XXX [2, 1995], 38.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Harmony relates to the
biblical-systematic hermeneutic discussed in Appropriating Scripture. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **A concrete example
of context appears in the routing of roads in southeastern Kansas. At one point,
a driver is on West 57, East 160, and North 69 all at the same time. A similar
thing happens near Russellville, Arkansas, and other places. Context shapes the
meaning of terms because the contextual subject shifts a word from one
application to another. The word <i>drink</i> used intransitively means to
drink liquor; transitively it means whatever liquid specified by the direct
object. <i>Affair</i> in the context of a man-woman relationship means sexual
involvement by married persons; otherwise, it means any occurrence with
something of a negative tone.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  The need for consistency
in interpretation can show up in seemingly innocuous matters. **For example, if
we suppose that the twelve were included in the seventy, we implicitly commit ourselves
to the possibility of apostasy, because Judas is called the Son of perdition
even though Jesus told the seventy when they returned that they should rejoice
because their names were written in heaven.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Foreign to the context means that,
while not contradictory to what is said, a suggested idea does not <u>arise</u>
from the surrounding text. It does not belong with the subject at hand. Statements
should be understood in a way that most enhances the flow of thought. In
Hebrews <b>7</b>:8, for example, Christ as the object of tithing brings in an
element foreign to the writers flow of thought: <i>There, one of whom it is
witnessed that he lives,</i> <i>i.e</i>., Melchizedek.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Keeping statements connected with
their contexts helps avoid the problem of proof-texting. Statements detached
from their setting take on plausible meanings, because the discussion forms a
new context that shapes their meaning. Proof-texting is illegitimate because it
uses a statement irrespective of its context and noted subject. New content is
poured into the extracted words by virtue of the external thought construction
of the interpreter; they are re-contextualized. </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>Genesis<b> 2</b>:3, written to Jews, can
be combined with Hebrews <b>4</b>:8 to prove that Saturday is the day Christians
should use for worship. Malachi <b>3</b>:10, written again to Jews, is often
misused to show that Christians are expected to tithe.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Proof-texting comes from taking
statements in more than one way</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>.
For example, someone might say, <i>Everyone falls short of the glory of God</i>
(Romans <b>3</b>:23). The sentence can mean two things: first, at some time or
other every person sins. (The characteristic present means that it happens
characteristically to everybody.) Second, people continue to fall short of the
glory of God. (The characteristic present lies in the ongoing pattern within the
same person.) The first is distributive; the second is characteristic. Both
ideas are possible ways of understanding Pauls statement. Readers
automatically choose one or the other meaning, depending on the topic in mind when
they read it. The first one comes to mind if a person is concerned with the
universal need for salvation. The second comes to mind if a person wants to
argue against perfectionism.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Proof-texting does not refer to combining
material from various authors and lines of tradition within scripture,
because scripture derives essentially from one Author. It refers to applying a
text to a subject the reader brings to it in contrast to the subject already
there in the context.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The importance of historical context
for interpretation can be seen in the gospels because contemporary Judaism
anticipated a political Messianic kingdom. As a result, Jesus statements
probably contrast with that belief wherever it is natural to do soat least
more so than he would without that realization. Furthermore, since Jesus
ministry occurred during the jurisdiction of the Mosaic law, some of his
statements were directed to the Jews in that setting, but they were not
intended to apply to non-Jewish Christians in the church age (cp. what it
means above under meaning of <i>interpret</i>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The law of harmony involves taking
the <u>ambiguous in the light of the clear</u>. Statements in certain passages
could be taken in the way someone is suggesting, but that understanding would controvert
clear teaching elsewhere. Harmony involves treating <u>the situational in light
of the general</u>, situational being either local <i>vs.</i> general or
temporary <i>vs.</i> permanent. Both situational possibilities are Pauls
directives on womens roles at home and church. Situations may be exceptional
because they bring in fundamental considerations that warrant overriding normal
procedure. Situations may be exceptional because practical considerations
dictate expediency considerations that would not apply to most cases.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  1. Analogy of scripture</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  <i>Scripture interprets scripture.</i>
How the New Testament handles Old Testament texts is a case in point. In some
parables Jesus explains the meaning. Other places in scripture deal with the
same topic, as in the case of Pauls doctrine of faith and works, found both in
Romans and Galatians. Analogy of scripture means that different texts treat
an issue the same way. It means letting the rest of revelation influence the
understanding of this part that might be unclear in itself. It means not
treating passages in isolation from each other.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  2. Gestalt</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  <i>The whole is more than the
sum of its parts.</i> Part-to-whole relationship has a qualifying effect on
the potential meaning of a statement because it shaves off possible ways of
taking an expression and limits it to what fits with the big picture. The whole
is not before the parts or the parts before the whole. The whole and the parts
are equally present; the parts make up the whole and the whole shapes the force
of the parts and gives them coherence. <b>One recurring problem in Bible study
is trying to work with parts aside from the whole</b>. Perhaps chapter and
verse divisions foster this difficulty. Bible studies can be structured around
reading one verse and commenting on it, reading the next and commenting on it.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 3. Examples of decontextualization
and recontextualization</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Texts are not to be read as if
each verse were a proverb and for that reason amounted to a generality. Proverbs
are short, pithy sayings that do not form part of a running context. They are
one-liners. But most literary genres are not of that sort nor are they to be
handled in that way.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**Preachers can take the foolishness of preaching (1
Corinthians <b>1</b>:21) to mean pulpit proclamation and then use it to plug
the located ministry. Actually, the foolishness has to do with the thing
preachedthe message, not the work of preaching.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **the whole
gospel (Acts<b> 20</b>:27)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (1) Interpreters
sometimes use this expression to contrast themselves with others who do not
consider water baptism to be connected with salvation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (2) Others
use this phrase to advocate seeking the tongue-speaking </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> Experience
(glossolalia). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (3) Still
others use it in reference to the doctrine of entire </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> sanctification.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (4) Paul
probably meant the whole gospel he preached in contrast to the Judaizers claim
that Gentiles needed to do morethey needed to become Jews by being circumcised
and keeping the Law of Moses. Perhaps he meant his gospel in contrast to
Gnostic claims to have secret knowledge.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:0in;
line-height:12.0pt'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Arial",sans-serif'>4.
<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>Correlative terms</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  In cases of correlative terms,
the sense in which one term in a set is meant is the sense also in which the
other term in the pair is meant: </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>father-son (physical or spiritual)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  prophecy-fulfillment</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  faith-works </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  teach-learn (1
Corinthians <b>14</b>:35; 1 Timothy<b> 2</b>:11)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  lost-saved</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  healed-diseased</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  headship-submission:
In this subject head cannot mean source rather than authority, as some suppose,
because source does not contrast naturally with submit.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  spirit-flesh: if
transcendent, then imminent; if figurative, then literal; if intangible, then
tangible; if incorruptible, then corruptible</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> speak in languagesinterpret
languages; </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>[<i>hermneu</i>] means translate when paired with </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>glssa</i>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  Adam-Christ</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  revelation-illumination</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  B. Law of negation (dialectic) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The law of negation is also called
the law of opposition, the law of contrast, the law of contradiction, the
law of exclusion. The law of negation means that statements are clearest when
seen in contrast to parallel alternatives. What a term contrasts with shapes what
it means, because it is placed in a common larger category with what it
negates. As a result, the law of negation is an aspect of the law of harmony. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  There is always a need to read
writings in light of their intended alternatives. (a) This approach is natural
in <u>all uses of human language</u> by the very nature of how thought and language.
The requirements of a specific communication are often more precise than the
verbiage current in the language; so speakers rely on context to specialize the
meaning of what they say. More than that, (b) in the <u>New Testament</u> many
books are a problem-solution writing. They were written to correct difficulties
in churches. Those errors and difficulties are that over against which the
books statements are to be understood.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The law of contrast affects <u>statements</u>
and <u>concepts</u>. It affects the way people emphasize words in a text, and
it affects the way they conceptualize particular ideas. English speakers
indicate that they are intentionally contrasting by stressing the specific word
and raising the pitch somewhat.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  One reason truths new to people are
so meaningful is that they can still feel the contrast with the misunderstandings
they had before.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> Non-instrumentalist
writers use the law of exclusion and combine it with necessary inference in
arguing that silence amounts to prohibition in matters of worship.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  1. English examples of the law of
contrast</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**cash <i>vs.</i> <u>check</u>, or <u>charge</u>, or <u>coins</u>,
or <u>bartering</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  credit <i>vs.</i>
cash, debit, discredit</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  The return
address corner of the return envelope for <i>World Book Direct Marketing</i>
(annual volume) used to say, Please Print. That does not mean that a payer
cannot use a return address sticker. We conclude that from the nature of the
case and the common knowledge that handwriting is often illegible; the
direction reads as it does in contrast to illegibility.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>Worship at
the church of your choice. In America we can worship as we please.</i> People
miss the point if say, <i>No, worship at the church of <u>Gods</u> choice</i>;
<i>No, worship as <u>God</u> pleases.</i> The sentences stand in contrast
with governmental control of worship or are intended as encouragements to
worshipyou are free to do so wherever you decide. They are not calculated to
contrast with a desire for truth or divine preference.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **hard <i>vs.</i>
<u>soft</u>, or <u>easy</u>, or <u>slightly</u> (<i>I worked hard</i>; <i>I
turned the wheel </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> hard to
the left.</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>), or <u>insensitive</u>
(<i>He is a hard man.</i>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **old <i>vs.</i>
<u>new</u>, or <u>young</u>, or <u>different</u>, or <u>fresh</u>, or <u>modern</u>
(rather than </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  traditional)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Come in!
(allowance) <i>vs.</i> Come in! (command)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Help
yourself (allowance) <i>vs.</i> Help yourself (nobody else will)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<u>Nights</u>
are for sleeping. (<i>vs.</i> sacking out in the daytime)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   Nights are for <u>sleeping</u>.
(<i>vs.</i> working)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i><u>What</u>
in the world are you doing? </i>The statement can be read with </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  different
meanings by stressing a different word each time.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**government furtherance of religion <i>vs.</i> <u>no
state church</u>, or <u>allowing </u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> <u>religion
an open forum</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **basketball <i>vs.</i>
<u>softball</u>, or <u>make-it-take-it</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Use India
ink. <i>vs.</i> <u>other kinds of ink</u>, or in contrast to <u>typing</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **street light: walk
<i>vs. </i><u>run</u>, or <u>do not walk</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **practical <i>vs.</i>
<u>impractical</u>, or <u>theoretical</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **parking <i>vs.</i>
<u>standing</u>, or no <u>parking</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Print your
name. <i>vs.</i> <u>write</u>, or <u>type</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **right <i>vs.</i>
<u>wrong</u>, or <u>left</u> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  2. Biblical examples of the law of contrast</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  In Bible reading, it is
important to stress the right words. Stressing a word (a) changes the meaning,
(b) shows that it is important, and (c) draws attention to it as the point of
contrast. Since reading passages with different stresses can shape
interpretation significantly, readers must decide whether the statement is
contrastive or positive; and if contrastive, which segment should receive the
emphasis to mark the contrast.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**Genesis <b>1</b>:11, 12, 21, 24, 25: after their kind
<i>vs.</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (1)
speciation (non-evolutionary change)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (2)
getting grapes from thorns and figs from thistles</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (3) Gods
having to create new ones directly when old ones wear out </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Genesis <b>2</b>:3
should read with a stress on <u>seventh</u> rather than no stress at all: <i>Therefore,
God blessed the <u>seventh</u> day and hallowed it because in it <u>he</u>
rested from all his work that God had created and made.</i> Moses wrote this as
a comment into his account of the creation from the standpoint of his own
chronological perspective, not from the time perspective of the creation event.
The reason there was a rest day was to memorialize of the exodus (Deuteronomy <b>5</b>:15);
the manner of observing it (<u>how</u>) was on the analogy of the presentation
about Gods creation rest. Without the emphasis, the text more easily lends
itself to the meaning Sabbatarians associate with it, namely, that the reason
for the rest day as well as the manner of observing the rest day both derive
from the creation event; so it is permanently to be observed.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  ** Proverbs <b>23</b>:23
is not a basis for not charging for <i>Christian literature</i>. Not sell it
contrasts with buying it, a figure for getting it. Selling means getting rid
of it rather than not charging for it.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Ezekiel <b>18</b>:20:
<i>The <u>soul that sins</u> will die</i> <i>vs.</i> <i>The soul that sins
will</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> <u>die</u>.</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew<b> 2</b>:4
should probably read, <i></i>[Herod]<i> asked [all the chief priests and
scribes] where <u>the Christ</u> would be born.</i> The Magi had simply asked
where the king of the Jews had been born. Herod evidently thought of the
Messiah when they used that phraseology, although king of the Jews may have
been understood as a messianic title: it is the same expression Pilate put as
the superscription on the cross later (Matthew <b>27</b>:37, 29, 42; Mark <b>15</b>:26;
Luke <b>23</b>:38; John <b>19</b>:19).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**Matthew<b> 5</b>:38-42: turn the other cheek <i>vs.</i>
(1) self-protection/pacifism, or (2) a pugnacious spirit/aggression. In Matthew<b>
5</b>:39 <i>turning the other cheek</i> contrasts with the law of revenge. The
notion of pacifism is possible only if you take the expression as a positive
statement without making it a corrective on eye for an eye used to justify
revenge. <i>Turning the other cheek</i> means pacifism if you put it in that
context, but Jesus frame of reference is social relationships, where revenge
does not belong.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew <b>6</b>:2,
5, 16; Luke <b>6</b>:24: <i>Do not pray like the Pharisees; they have <u>their</u>
reward vs. They <u>have</u> their reward.</i> The last option may fit best
with the Luke <b>6</b>:24 parallel.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew <b>6</b>:4,
6, 16: Doing righteousness <u>in secret</u> contrasts with doing it <u>to be
seen</u> by other people. The statements are not calculated to forbid public
prayer, public giving, or group fasting. To be seen shows that Jesus is
concerned about the <u>motive</u>. Doing these righteous acts in secret would
avoid that problem; it is the motive that a person would have in doing it in
secret that should be present in public as well.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew <b>23</b>:15:
<i>. . . make a <u>Gentile</u> twofold more the child of hell than
yourselves. vs. . . . make a Gentile twofold <u>more</u> the child of hell
than yourselves.</i> The point is not that the Gentiles are saved in their
ignorance.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew <b>24</b>:36:
<i>. . . but of <u>that</u> day and hour vs. . . . but of that <u>day and
hour</u>. <u>That</u> day and hour</i> evidently refers to the day and hour
of the second coming in contrast to the time of the destruction of Jerusalem. The
contrast is not with<b> 24</b>:41, 44, because day and hour are in the same
context as a combination (<b>24</b>:36 + 50). The contrast is not then between
a general time and a specific day and hour.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew <b>28</b>:18:
go <i>vs.</i> <u>stay</u>, or <u>come</u>, or <u>wait</u> (for the world to
come to </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> you)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Mark <b>10</b>:45:
ransom for many <i>vs.</i> <u>all</u>, or <u>one</u> (Romans<b> 5</b>:18; Mark <b>10</b>:45),
or <u>few</u> (Matthew <b>22</b>:14; Revelation <b>17</b>:14; 2 Peter <b>1</b>:10)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Luke <b>15</b>:29:
<i>You never gave <u>me</u> a kid that I might make merry with my friends. vs.
You never gave me a <u>kid</u> that I might make merry with my friends</i> (the
correct reading since the father had not given the prodigal a <u>calf</u>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Luke <b>17</b>:20:
<i>The kingdom of God does not come with observation vs.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
(1) invisible kingdom that a person cannot see come</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
(2) military-type kingdom observably established by military means and having
geographical dimensions   </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Luke <b>22</b>:15:
<i>I have certainly desired to eat <u>this</u> Passover with you before I
suffer . . . because . . . I will not eat it until it is fulfilled in the
kingdom of God.</i> At least conceptually emphasizing <u>this</u>
differentiates between this Passover and the previous ones because it was his
last one and was so near to his own sacrificial suffering.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **John <b>1</b>:9:
<i><u>He</u> was the true light that enlightens every man</i> (<i>vs.</i>
some other savior); He was the true light that enlightens <u>every</u> man (<i>vs.</i>
limited atonement); <i>He was the true light that enlightens everyone</i> (a
positive, non-contrasting statement that depicts the Word as light).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **John <b>3</b>:16:
God loved the world <i>vs.</i> <u>heaven</u>, or <u>Jews only</u> (Calvinistic </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  interpretation)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>The following context individualizes the
affirmation: <i>he that believes</i> (<b>3</b>:18); <i>people loved
darkness</i> (<b>3</b>:19); <i>everyone that does evil</i> (<b>3</b>:20); <i>he
that does truth</i> (<b>3</b>:21). Jew-Gentile is not a contextual
distinction; hence, there is no basis for bringing it into the context.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **In John<b> 6</b>:44
the stress needs to be kept on <u>Father</u> in contrast to being <u>drawn</u>
by someone else. The issue here is who is doing the drawingthe Father or the
devil; so the stress does not fall on <u>draw</u> as to if to imply that you
cannot come if God does not decide to draw you or make you able to be drawn<i>:
No one can come to me except the <u>Father that sent me</u> draw him</i> (but
note <b>6</b>:65). <u>Draw</u> contrasts with <u>drive</u>. (Note concept of
leadership.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **John <b>14</b>:9:
<i>Have <u>I</u> not been so long time with you, Philip, and you have not seen
<u>me</u>? He that has seen <u>me</u> has seen the <u>Father</u>. vs.</i> <i>He
that has seen <u>me</u> has <u>seen</u> the Father.</i> The latter reading
makes it sound moe like Jesus and the Father are the same one. Jesus point
with Philip, however, is that seeing <u>Jesus</u> is as good as seeing the
Father. If a person has seen <u>him</u>, he knows close enough what the Father
is like; he knows as well as a person could know in this life what deity is
like.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **When Acts <b>2</b>:38;<b>
8</b>:16; <b>10</b>:48; Romans<b> 6</b>:3; Galatians <b>3</b>:27 say <i>baptized
in/into (the name of) Jesus/Christ,</i> they are making positive statements
rather than contrastive ones. Consequently, they are not to be put in opposition
to Matthew <b>28</b>:18-20. Particularly is this true of Acts<b> 8</b>:16: only
they had been baptized in the name of Jesus (Does only go with <u>Jesus</u>
or with <u>baptized</u>?) <i>vs.</i> <u>receiving the Holy Spirit</u> (Acts <b>8</b>:16),
or <u>baptism of John</u> (Acts <b>19</b>:5), or <u>not being baptized</u>
(Romans <b>6</b>:3; Galatians <b>3</b>:27). Obviously, at the very general
level, <i>baptism into the name of Jesus Christ</i> means identification with
Christ in contrast to all other parallel possibilities; but baptism into the
name of the Father or baptism into the name of the Spirit is not a parallel
possibility since Father-Son-Spirit are one, or at one.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Romans<b> 1</b>:27:
<i>. . . leaving the <u>natural</u> use of the woman vs. . . . leaving the
natural use of the <u>woman</u>. </i>The latter is the preferred reading
because Paul is dealing with homosexuality. <i>Natural</i> is a non-restrictive
adjective in this case.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Romans<b> 5</b>:12ff.:
Adam is not a biological category because it contrasts with Christ/Second
Adam, which is not a biological category. Consequently, Paul does not say or
assume or imply that men are physically born into Adam any more than they are
physically born into Christ.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Romans <b>8</b>:39
should be read <i>. . . nor any other <u>creature</u></i> rather than <i>nor
any <u>other</u> creature,</i> because the contrast is not between kinds of
creatures.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Romans <b>12</b>:18
says, <i>As much as lies in <u>you</u>, live at peace with all men</i> (read
as indicating that since two parties are involved, one party cannot guarantee
peace). Read without emphasis, the statement simply exhorts readers to try as
hard as they can to live at peace with all men by not taking vengeance, and so
on. Read with this emphasis, the passage assumes that Paul recognized that a
relationship problem cannot be solved entirely from one side.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Romans <b>14</b>:7:
people do not live or die to themselves equals a comment on the fact that we know
each other is watching</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> = we do
not live merely as <u>we</u> please</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Romans <b>15</b>:12:
<i>And again <u>Isaiah</u> says . . .</i> The emphasis should not go on <u>again</u>
because the previous quotation is not from Isaiah, but from the Psalms.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**1 Corinthians <b>7</b>:15: in such cases <i>vs.</i> in
<u>such</u> cases (<b>7</b>:11 remain unmarried; <b>7</b>:15 means is not
bound in <u>such</u> cases so as to imply that when the unbeliever leaves, the
believer is not bound in contrast to when the believer leaves. The believer <u>is</u>
bound in such cases if he initiates the leaving.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Corinthians <b>7</b>:27
says, <i>Are you loosed from a wife?</i> Is it loosed <i>vs.</i> bound
meaning <u>divorced-unmarried</u>, or <u>simply unmarried</u>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Corinthians <b>11</b>:21:
Drunken (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>, <i>methyei</i>) contrasts with hungry
and associated with both eating and drinking; hence, it may mean satiated or
stuffed.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:17:
<i><u>You</u> are giving thanks all right, but the other person is not being
edified.</i> With the stress on <i>you</i> the text makes a point of the
difference between the tongue speakers meaningful communication and the lack
of meaningfulness going on in the hearer. The pronoun is separately expressed
in the original.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **In 1
Corinthians<b> 14</b>:19, 35 does in church contrast with at home, in </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  private,
or in evangelism?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Corinthians<b>
15</b>:7 recounts<i>, Then he appeared to James and then to <u>all</u> the
apostles vs. . . . all the <u>apostles</u>. </i><u>All</u> is stressed if
James is considered among the apostles; otherwise, <u>apostles</u> is stressed.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Corinthians<b>
15</b>:44: physical <i>vs.</i> spiritual</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **2 Corinthians<b>
5</b>:8 puts faith in contrast to sight (cp. Hebrews <b>11</b>:1-3, 7, 27; 1
Peter <b>1</b>:8), not knowledge as if the issue were a matter of degree of
certainty rather than one of epistemology.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Ephesians <b>4</b>:5:
one baptism <i>vs.</i> (1) one baptism for Jews and one for </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  
Gentiles</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  
 (2) three modes of baptism</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
 (3) trine baptism</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   (4)
baptism in the Holy Spirit</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (5)
baptism of suffering/baptism of blood</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Colossians <b>1</b>:20:
<i>. . . in <u>him</u> to reconcile all things vs. . . . in him to </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  reconcile <u>all</u>
things</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Timothy <b>2</b>:11-12:
be in quietness<i> vs.</i> have dominion</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Timothy <b>5</b>:1-2:
elderly women <i>vs.</i> <u>elders who are men</u>, or <u>younger women</u>.
The contrast is specified as being between </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>presbyters</i>, older) and </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>neters</i>, younger); hence <i>presbyters</i>
(older women) is not in contrast to <i>presbyterous</i> (older men) but in
contrast to those who might be called sisters <i>vs.</i> mothers. <i>. . . <u>older</u>
women as mothers and <u>younger</u> women as sisters. </i>The contrast is not
between women and men (elders) or between mothers and sisters. It is a matter
of age that informs the contrasts.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **2 Timothy <b>3</b>:16
says, <i>All scripture, given by inspiration of God, (is) also profitable. vs.
All scripture given by inspiration of God is also profitable.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Hebrews <b>6</b>:5:
<i>tasted of the heavenly gift</i> <i>vs.</i> (1) swallow</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
(2) imperceptive experience</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**<i>Everyone that <u>loves</u> is begotten by God </i>(1
John <b>4</b>:7). Putting stress on <u>love</u> makes a contrast here with the
emphasis on <u>knowledge</u> as found in Gnosticism. The person who puts
emphasis on love rather than knowledge is the one that is saved. It is the lover
not the knower who is saved. Without stress the text would make a positive,
non-contrastive statement that implies that all those who love are saved
people. When we say that those who <u>love</u> are begotten by God rather than
those who <u>know</u>, we do not mean to say that <u>all</u> who love are
begotten by God. When we say that something is true (salvation) of a category
(loving) in contrast to another category (unloving), we do not mean to say that
every example in that category (loving) has that characteristic (salvation).
Johns comment about love could apply to the Stoic or Encratic type of Gnosticism
as well, because distancing themselves from the material realm translated
psychologically into a superiority attitude, hence, the relevance of comments
about hate, despair, looking down on a brother (who marries, <i>e.g</i>.). In
the direction of Epicurean, or libertine, Gnosticism, the love corrective ties
in with the notion that being begotten by God means a person does not
characteristically sin, whereas among libertines the regenerated ones were
not concerned about ceasing from characteristic sinning.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **In Hebrews <b>5-7</b>
the recurring quotation of Psalm <b>110</b>:4 receives a different stress at
different times when the Hebrew writer uses it: <i>priest</i> is stressed in <b>5</b>:6,
10; <i>Melchizedek</i>, in <b>6</b>:20; <i>forever</i>, in <b>7</b>:17; and <i>swore</i>,
in <b>7</b>:21.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **faith <i>vs.</i>
works faith <i><u>vs.</u></i> works (Paul: works of law <i>vs.</i> <u>trust</u>
in a person)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
faith as a work (John<b> 6</b>:29)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
faith and works (James <b>2</b>: works [doing] <i>vs.</i> <u>believing</u>) James
is not contrasting two kinds of faithone that works <i>vs.</i> one that does
not. Consequently, James point should not be read as dealing with a faith that
works (<i>vs.</i> one that does not work), but as dealing with faith alone <i>vs.</i>
faith and works together.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
faith as inclusive of action (Luke <b>16</b>:10)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **spirit <i>vs.</i>
(1) letter (intended meaning of words?): 2 Corinthians<b> 3</b>:6</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   (2)
soul: 1 Thessalonians<b> 5</b>:23; Hebrews<b> 4</b>:12</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   (3)
real: 1 Corinthians <b>5</b>:3</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
(4) Father and Son: John <b>14</b>:16</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (5)
flesh: Galatians <b>5</b>:16-24;<b> 6</b>:8. <i>Walk by the spirit and you </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   will
not be fulfilling the desires of the flesh,</span></i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> and so on.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (6)
understand: 1 Corinthians<b> 14</b>:15</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  1
Corinthians <b>15</b>:50: Flesh and blood cannot inherit the </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
  kingdom of God, but people can </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> receive
a spiritual body.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:274.5pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-256.5pt;
line-height:12.0pt'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
 Galatians <b>4</b>:21-31:  The Hagar-Sarah contrast
parallels a law-grace and flesh-spirit contrast.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
John <b>3</b>:3-15: born of the water/spirit <i>vs.</i> born of the flesh </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
Matthew <b>26</b>:41:<i> the spirit is willing, but the flesh is weak. </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  When <i>spirit</i>
contrasts with Father and Son, it is natural to capitalize it. When it stands
in contrast to <i>letter</i>, <i>soul</i>, <i>real</i>, and <i>flesh</i>, it is
best not to capitalize it.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>The spirit-flesh contrast encompasses
physical and political (Israel) and legal (works) because a political nation operates
by a legal system and physical people make it up. Much of the use of <i>spirit</i>
in the New Testament ends up amounting to interpersonal. The Great Commission
is, then, a directive to proclaim a message to people so as to win them by
persuasion rather than a commission to make war on the nations to force them to
become followers of the true God.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  James <b>5</b>:13-20
has been taken by some to mean a contrast between praying for <u>physical
healing</u> yourself <i>vs.</i> calling the elders of the church for misfortune
in circumstances or spiritual condition.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew
regularly substitutes kingdom of <u>heaven</u> for kingdom of God in the
other synoptics perhaps to emphasize the non-political nature of the Messianic
kingdom (heaven could also be a euphemism for God; note Luke <b>15</b>:18, 21).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Israel <i>vs</i>
<u>Egypt</u>, or <u>Esau</u>, or <u>Judah</u>, or <u>church</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **hate <i>vs.</i>
love: hate = a negative term  (ex. Jacob I loved; Esau I hated;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
hate = neutral term  Jacob loved Rachel, hated Leah;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> 
 Love God; hate father and mother.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> The two
alternatives have in common the lack of psychologically being drawn to a
person. Antonyms are used to affirm the lesser rather than the opposite.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **In <i>De
magistro</i> <i>1</i>, Augustine fails to apply the law of contrast properly
when he takes the secret closet to mean the mind, despite Jesus contrasting it
with praying on the street corner.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **In the Golden
Rule (which equals the Second Great Commandment), love includes both inner and
outer factors: the attitude of the heart and the characteristic behavior that
issues from it. Pauls ode to love in 1 Corinthians <b>13</b> indicates the
patterns of behavior that flow from the right inner disposition.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> <b>One of two big issues in the
New Testament</b> is</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<b>(1) the
nature of the kingdom as interpersonal <i>vs.</i> political (the Jewish
expectancy/legal). </b>Jesus parables of the kingdom contrast with the
prevailing view of Judaism, which Jesus was trying to correct through storytelling.
The kingdom of heaven is to be received as a little child in contrast to
military-political process and trying to enter into the kingdom of heaven by
force. People cannot bring in the Messianic kingdom by force; they cannot
establish it militarily. <i>Everybody since John is trying to take the kingdom
by force</i> contrasts with receiving it the way a little child receives
