things. As per the law of opposition, the kingdom of heaven is <u>interpersonal</u>
in kind, operation, origin, and growth (<u>influence</u>). These features
contrasted with Jewish expectancy of a kingdom that was of a <u>political</u>
sort, carried on by <u>legal</u> processes, and established and spread by <u>military</u>
operations. In one kingdom parable, Jesus told about a man that planted seed
but did not know how it grew and bore fruit. In contrast to military expansion,
the spread of the gospel is natural, somewhat automatic, and in a way
mysterious. It goes forward <u>by degrees</u> (<i>vs.</i> a military takeover at
a given time) both in its spread and depth; its spread is a <u>mystery</u>
(knows not how), <u>deliberate</u> (planted the seed), yet <u>automatic</u>
(bears fruit of itself).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><b><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**(2) <b>the nature of salvation as interpersonal
<i>vs.</i> epistemological/ ontological (Gnosticism/informational). </b>The
interpersonal <i>vs.</i> political nature of the Messianic kingdom in <i>ecclesiology
</i>correlates with salvation by faith <i>vs.</i> works in <i>soteriology</i>. Peoples
being in the kingdom and their place within the kingdom are not the result of force.
Appropriately, circumcision was a physical mark of membership in a
physical-political-national kingdom, but baptism as an act of faith for
identifying with Christ is the correlating mark of membership in a
spiritual-interpersonal kingdom.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>g</i>) <i>vs.</i> <i>sea</i> is translated land. 
 </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
color:#7030A0'>vs.</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> <i>sun</i>
is translated earth.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>Heaven</i> <i>vs.</i>
<i>earth</i> means sky. In contrast to sky, it means Gods </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> dwelling place. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **The Bible
contains some rhetorically nice statements of contrast, </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  especially
in the Book of Hebrews: <b>1</b>:1-2; <b>7</b>:16; <b>9</b>:13-14.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  3. Words and phrases can be used
positively rather than contrastingly; a statement may be <u>positive rather
than restrictive</u>. They are positive in the sense that they are not
consciously contrastive or restrictive. A positive statement implies nothing
about whether the point made is also true outside the category the speaker is
addressing. When speakers stress a word or sentence element not meant to be
stressed, they commit the fallacy of accent. By stressing the word, they make
it contrastive and therefore restrictive (<i>vs.</i> non-restrictive) and
technical. Interpreters have to distinguish restrictive and non-restrictive
statements. They do so by the law of harmony plus the nature of the case. The
issue applies to non-restrictive nouns, adjectives, adverbs as well as relative
clauses, adverbial clauses, and prepositional phrases.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**Proverbs <b>13</b>:24: Spare the <u>rod</u> and spoil
the child (the idea that parents should use a rod instead of a paddle or
switch when disciplining their children)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Proverbs<b> 22</b>:6:
<i>Train up a child in the way he should go . . .</i> <i>vs.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> <i>
Train up a child in the way <u>he</u> should go . . . </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>This verse has been used to say that a
person should not try to make a child into a personality type that is not
natural for the child. There is not a separate pronoun expressed in the Hebrew
for <i>he</i>. Whatever may be true about this idea, it is not the point of the
text.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  During the
period of the divided kingdom, <u>Israel</u> became the technical term for the
northern kingdom and <u>Judah</u> became the technical term for the southern
kingdom. Outside of this setting, however, there is no reason to suppose an
intended distinction between the terms.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Jeremiah <b>7</b>:22
says, <i>I did not speak to <u>your</u> fathers about sacrifices when I
brought them out of Egypt. </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>You have
oppressed the stranger <u>wrongfully</u> </i>(Ezekiel <b>22</b>:29). Oppressing
a stranger could not be other than wrong. Wrongfully re-enforces the idea
carried already in the verb. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew <b>5</b>:43<i>:
Love your <u>neighbor</u> as yourself. vs.</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (1)
personal enemy</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (2)
non-Jew (Parable of the Good Samaritan)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (3)
neighbors (The idea is supposed to be that the Christian should select </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  <u>one</u>
neighbor and concentrate on that person as the object of love.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (4) <i>Love
your neighbor as yourself</i> as a non-contrasting statement.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  The
second great commandment was originally given within the framework of the
nation of Israel. To use it then in contrast to Gentiles is foreign to the
frame of reference; that is, non-Jews are not in view at all. Obviously, the
singular is not in contrast to a plural; it is a positive rather than contrastive
statement. Jesus means neighbor in a kind-of-person sense rather than as an
identity.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Acts<b> 2</b>:29
could be read <i>and <u>his</u></i> [Davids in contrast to Christs] <i>tomb
is </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  with us to
this day.</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**Acts <b>19</b>:2<b>: </b><i>Did you receive the <u>Holy
Spirit</u> when you believed?</i> <i>vs.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  <i>Did
you receive the Holy Spirit when you <u>believed</u>?</i> (taken to argue that
a person can also receive the Holy Spirit before or after baptism). Paul is
referring to some time back; hence, he is not contrasting times that are very
close together as would be the case between the time of believing and the time
of being baptized.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  The we
passages in Acts do not imply that the author was with Paul only on the
occasions where we occurs,  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Romans<b> 1</b>:27:
<i>the natural use of the woman</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  Romans <b>16</b>:16:
Culture-bound imperatives are all non-restrictive statements: Salute each
other with a holy kiss.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Corinthians<b>
11</b>:7: <u>Man</u> is in the image and glory of God, but the woman is the
glory of the man. Is woman not in the image of God? Is woman indirectly in the
image of God because of being created after and from the man? Genesis<b> 1</b>:26-27
seems to put image at the corporate level; Paul would be putting it at the
individual level.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Theologians
sometimes use 1 Corinthians <b>15</b>:3 to argue for limited atonement: <i>Christ
died for our sins according to the scriptures</i> (<i>vs.</i> dying for
everyones sins). That contrastive take is by no means a necessary reading of
the verse; consequently, it is by no means a basis for espousing definite
atonement. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **2 Corinthians.
<b>6</b>:14: <i>Do not be <u>unequally</u> yoked together with unbelievers.</i>
The point is not that we can be equally yoked with them, but that being yoked
with unbelievers is an unequal situation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Ephesians <b>5</b>:19:
<i>Speaking to one another in hymns . . . making melody in </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  your <u>heart</u></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Timothy<b> 3</b>:8:
<i>not given to <u>much</u> wine</i> <i>vs.</i> a little wine is okay (for deacons)not
a contrasting statement</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Does 1 Timothy
<b>5</b>:23 forbid the use of anything but wine for stomach </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  troubles and
infirmities?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Timothy <b>6</b>:17-21:
<i>Charge them that are rich in the present world that they not . . . have
their hope set on <u>uncertain</u> riches</i> (KJV). The commandment is not
calculated to approve sure-fire investments only.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  Hebrews <b>12</b>:1:
<i>lay aside . . . the easily besetting sin</i> surely means to lay aside
sin, which so easily besets us, not <u>just</u> the sin that easily besets and
let the rest go. Sin easily besets in the real testing times of life.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**<i>To the one that knows to do good and does not do itit
is sin </i>(James <b>4</b>:17). Restrictively read, this passage implies that
only those who know to do good have sin reckoned against them. Non-restrictively
read, it might mean that the author has the knowing-to-do-good people in mind
and those not knowing are simply not in mind for the moment. He may mean it is
doubly natural for the knowing to be regarded as sinners.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  Does James <b>5</b>:14
forbid calling a doctor when we are sick? It says call the </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  elders of
the church.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Revelation <b>1</b>:1,
4, 9-10: John the <u>prophet</u> <i>vs.</i> John the <u>elder</u> (2 John <b>1</b>;
3 John <b>1</b>). This passage represents a technical <i>vs.</i> general usage
of terms <i>prophet </i>and <i>elders</i>. Decisions on this point here affect
the authorship question on the Apocalypse.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<u>Situations</u>
can also be contrastive or non-contrastive. An adult Bible class voted to send
$100 to a campus ministry. A couple months earlier they had voted to send $50
to a Christian college. That does not mean they appreciated the campus ministry
more than the college, because the one situation was not decided in light of
the other. Such cases can offend people unnecessarily because they read them as
put-downs; they take it personally.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>He brought
his young wife to church with him. </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   <i>He bought
his beautiful wife a rose.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Young people
ought to pay attention to adults, who know what young </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  people are up
against. <i>vs.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  <i>Young
people ought to pay attention to adults who know what young </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> people
are up against.</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>Disregard
the first two false readings. </i>This sign appeared on the heart-rate meter
at Kansas State Universitys recreation complex. The sign meant to disregard
the first two readings; they would be false; hence, it had a non-contrastive,
or non-restrictive, use of <i>false</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  4. Relative/limited/restrictive negative
(the existential fallacy)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Relative negative and absolute
negative are often worded the same way. It happens in biblical as well as
everyday speaking: (1) <u>a</u>-not-<u>b</u> has the sense of (2) not so
much <u>a</u> as <u>b</u> or (3) not only <u>a</u> but <u>b</u> also. Relative
negative is often cast in the form of absolute negative. By the nature of the
case, the hearer can usually tell that the meaning does not match the form of
expression. Sometimes <i>a</i> bears a part-to-whole relationship with <i>b</i>;
at other times <i>a</i> has a preliminary relationship to <i>b</i>, which
chronologically or logically succeeds it. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Relative negative can be
relative (a) because one factor is more important than another one in producing
an effect, (b) because one factor is more directly involved in producing it, or
(c) because one is the inspiring source of the other.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   **Matthew<b> 5</b>:17
may use relative negative when Jesus says, <i>I did not come to destroy the
law, but to fulfill it. </i>The uncertainty lies in the meaning of the word <i>destroy</i>.
Does it mean annul or treat as false?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Matthew <b>9</b>:13
(= Mark <b>12</b>:33) draws on Hosea <b>6</b>:6 (= 1 Samuel<b> 15</b>:22) to
say that God desires mercy, not sacrifice, when, as a matter of fact, God had
prescribed any number of sacrifices for the Israelites to observe. <i>I desire
mercy and not sacrifice</i> means <i>I desire mercy more than sacrificed
animals.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  ** In Matthew <b>9</b>:13
again, Jesus goes on to say that he did not come to call righteous people but
sinners to repentance. Obviously, there are no absolutely righteous people that
need no repentance, and so he called the relatively righteous to their
appropriate degree of repentance as well.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>It is not
[so much] you that speak, but the Spirit of your Father that speaks in you </i>(Matthew
<b>10</b>:20). (1) A not B would apparently mean here that the Holy Spirit
takes over the speech mechanisms. Meanings that fade into the two alternatives
would be (2a) repeating the audible words the speakers hear from the Spirit, or
(2b) expressing the ideas supernaturally placed in the mind by the Spirit, or
(2c) bringing to bear a truth believed from previous revelation, or (2d)
explaining ideas resulting from supernatural enablement of human abilities used
to analyze current experience. (cp. Five Models of a Completely Reliable
Text)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>I did not
come to send peace on the earth, but a sword </i>(Matthew </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> <b>10</b>:34;
note purpose-result conflation also).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **<i>Whoever receives me does not
[so much/just] receive me but him that </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> sent me </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>(Mark <b>9</b>:37). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Mark<b> 13</b>:11:
<i>You are not the ones speaking, but the Holy Spirit. </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>Do not
weep for me, but for your children </i>(Luke<b> 23</b>:28). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> Relative negative is a
way of handling the variant comments in Johns gospel as to whether Jesus came
into the world to judge it (John <b>3</b>:17; <b>12</b>:47; cp. <b>8</b>:15). He
did not so much, or primarily, or first, come into the world to condemn it, but
to save it. Rejection of that initial effort does lead to subsequent judgment
(as Gods back-up concern).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **John <b>4</b>:42:
<i>We do not believe because of your word, because we </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> ourselves
heard. . . .</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>You are
looking for me, not because you saw signs, but because you at some of the
loaves and were filled </i>(John<b> 6</b>:26:). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **John <b>7</b>:16
shows that limited negative can fade into direct-indirect at times: <i>My
teaching is not mine, but his that sent me </i>(cp. <b>14</b>:24).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>He that
believes on me, does not believe on me, but on him that sent me </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (John<b> 12</b>:44).
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>I did not
come to judge the world, but to save the world </i>(John <b>12</b>:47; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> cp.<b> 3</b>:17).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>The word
that you hear is not mine, but the Fathers who sent me </i>(John </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  <b>14</b>:24).
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>I do not
call you slaves/servants, but friends</i> in John <b>15</b>:15 must mean <i>I
do not so much call you servants as friends,</i> because elsewhere he <u>does</u>
call them servants and because his disciples did <u>not</u> know very muchmuch
less allthat Jesus was doing: <i>It is not for you to know the times and the
seasons. . . .</i> (Acts <b>1</b>:7).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**John <b>15</b>:16 says, <i>You did not choose me, but
I chose you. </i>Relative negative takes this to mean, <i>It is not so much
that you have chosen me as it is that I have chosen you.</i> In light of the
Messianic situation in contrast to the political-leader situation Jews
expected, Jesus statement better harks back to the special, individualized
calling Jesus extended to the twelve. In general, people make men their leaders
by willingness to follow them. Without the followers willingness to follow,
the leader would not be the leader. This situation is not exactly the case in
Messianic matters. The Christ is the leader by divine appointment. The only
question left is who is willing to follow. In other words, Christ does not need
followers to make him a leader, which is the unconscious approach people take
toward all leaders including a Messianic leader. Jesus ministry amounted to a
time, not in which he was trying to win the Messianic role, but in which he was
revealing himself as Messiah as per Gods call to him. Even here, there is the
choosing to follow him. In the case of the apostles, Jesus called them to be
his disciples, which did not necessarily have anything to do with their eternal
destinyremember Judas.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Peter tells
Ananias, <i>You have not lied to men, but to God </i>(Acts <b>5</b>:4).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>He is not
a Jew that is one outwardly; neither is it circumcision that is outward in the
flesh, but he is a Jew who is one inwardly; and circumcision is that of the
heartin the spirit, not in the letter, whose praise is not from men, but from
God </i>(Romans <b>2</b>:28-29).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  What would
happen if we put a relative negative between faith and works? <i>We are not so
much saved by what we do as by the other in whom we have placed our trust.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>Christ did
not send me to baptize, but to preach </i>(1 Corinthians<b> 1</b>:17; cp.
Matthew <b>28</b>:19-20). Another rendering may be preferable: <i>God did not
send me to perform baptisms.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>The
wife/husband does not have power over her/his own body, but the husband/wife
does </i>(1 Corinthians <b>7</b>:4). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Corinthians <b>9</b>:9:
<i>God does not [so much] care for oxen </i>[in making this commandment, as he
expresses concern for people]?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  On the basis of
Isaiah <b>28</b>:11-12, Paul says (1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:22) tongues are for
unbelievers and prophesying is for believers. He could mean it in a relative
negative sense: <i>Languages are particularly appropriate for unbelievers
while prophesying is particularly designed for believers. </i>The possibility
seems likely because of <b>14</b>:5, where he says that he is willing for them
all to speak in tongues, but he wants tongues to have the effect of prophesying
so the church may receive edification. Furthermore, the Old Testament citation
refers to foreigners speaking to Israel in foreign languages, not supernatural
languages. In Pauls mind, then, the apologetic force does not seem to lie in
the supernaturalness, but in the foreignness. The apostle proceeds to say that
unbelievers coming into a language-speaking situation will think the people are
crazy, even though he has just said that tongues were for unbelievers. So the
tongues-for-unbelievers point must lie in the fact that they do communicate to
the hearers if they understand them, but they create the adverse effect if hearers
do not understand them. The apologetic angle must relate to the idea that God
is standing on someone elses side, which is something perceived as much by the
content of the message (cp. prophesying) as by the foreignness of the languages
used to communicate it. (See Opposing Compatibles.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>I labored
more abundantly than they all, yet not I, but the grace of God that was with
me</i> (1 Corinthians<b> 15</b>:10).  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**2 Corinthians<b> 5</b>:7 says that we walk by faith,
not by sight, which implies that we know (how to walk) by trust in another
rather than by personal experience. We conduct our lives to a certain extent by
direct experience, but in regard to more things and at the level of the whole
we walk by trust in God.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>I have
been crucified with Christ; and it is no longer I that am living, but it is Christ
who is living in me </i>(Galatians<b> 2</b>:20). Pauls point is not
self-negation in the sense of self-annihilation. That would be more like an Eastern
religious concept.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>No man
ever hated his own flesh </i>(Ephesians<b> 5</b>:29). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>. . . each
of you not looking to your own things, but each of you looking also to the
things of others </i>(Philippians <b>2</b>:4).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>Therefore,
those who reject do not reject people, but God, who gives his Holy Spirit to
you </i>(1 Thessalonians <b>4</b>:8). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Is the
prohibition in 1Timothy<b> 2</b>:9 against the wearing of pearls and elaborate
hairstyles an example of limited negation?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **<i>No longer
be [so much] a drinker of water, but use a little wine for your stomachs sake
and for your frequent infirmities </i>(1 Timothy <b>5</b>:23). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 Peter <b>3</b>:3-4
says that a womans adorning should not be the outward adorning of hair, and so
on, but with the hidden qualities of the hearta quiet spirit: <i>Whose
adorning let not [so much] be the outward adorning of braiding the hair and
wearing jewels of gold or of putting on apparel, but let it be the hidden man
of the heart. . . .</i> This text <u>must</u> mean limited negative;
otherwise, Paul would be forbidding her to wear clothes.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **1 John <b>4</b>:10:
<i>Herein is love, not that we loved God, but that he loved </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> us.</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Jesus isnt
the reason for the season; he is the reason for every day.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **What
possibilities would there be for saying that salvation by faith not works is a
relative negative?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  5. Biblical interpretation needs to
deal with <u>technical <i>vs.</i> normal terminology</u>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Technicalizing terminology is
also called over-specialization. It takes terms in more specialized fashion
than normally meant; it is the opposite of under-specialization, which can
occur in periphrastic translation. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Two kinds of mistakes can
happen. (a) The author may be using a general term in a specialized way (<i>teach</i>
in 1 Timothy <b>2</b>:12, <i>e.g</i>.), while the reader may be reading him in
a generalizing way. (b) The author may be using a term in a general way (Romans
<b>16</b>:2), while the interpreter reads him in a specialized way.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
color:#7030A0'>  ** Best man in a wedding <i>vs.</i> May the best
man win illustrates technical </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  and general
usage. (See Pitfalls of Interpretation.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **apostle</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **elder</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **prophet</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **deacon</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **minister</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **teach (1
Timothy<b> 2</b>:12)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Relying too much on word
studies creates the impression that all the meaning is carried in the words and
under-regards syntax, context and systematic viewpoint. For this reason, resources
like the <i>Theological Dictionary of the New Testament</i> does not provide an
ultimate resource for dealing with matters of interpretation. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  6. Descriptors can be negative,
neutral, positive: immoral, amoral, moral; legal, </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> non-legal, illegal</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  7. Be careful about opposing
compatibles (dichotomizing) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Things treated as mutually
exclusive can be complementary truths that qualify one another and present a
more complete picture. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
color:#7030A0'>  **The old Miller Lite commercial where the
participants argued whether it </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>was less filling or tasted great.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Since fasting
is never done in scripture except as a religious exercise, someone might
conclude that it would be wrong to fast for other reasons like weight loss or as
an aid to developing self-control.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Because sex is
for procreation, some have concluded that sexual relationship without the
intent of procreation is contrary to nature and therefore sinful.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **To say that
tongues had apologetic purpose (1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:22) does not in itself
eliminate them from having edification value (<b>14</b>:5). 1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:22
could be a relative negative.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  **Wearing
jewelry, apparel, braided hair does not eliminate inner holiness (1 Timothy<b>
2</b>:9-10; 1 Peter <b>3</b>:3-6).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  What of Pauls
claim that the unmarried person pleases the Lord, and the married one pleases
the spouse (1 Corinthians <b>7</b>:32-35)?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  We need not put
in opposition items like interpersonalism and authority, interpersonalism and
force, justice and love. They can coexist as long as each is done in a way that
does not eliminate the other.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  People take
general principles as contradictions to practical exceptions: </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   (1) Mark and Luke have
no divorce clause while Matthew<b> 19</b> does;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  (2) Genesis <b>1</b>
supposedly shows husband and wife equal while Genesis <b>3</b> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> involves hierarchy;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   (3) Leadership by
interpersonal dynamics is put in opposition to hierarchical </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> arrangement. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   C. Nature of the case</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   Nature of the case requires <u>reality
thinking</u>. Reality thinking contrasts with (a) analogical reasoning and (b)
word-based argumentation. It is what people mean by not comparing apples and oranges.
Reality thinking helps avoid allegorizing and overly depending on the <u>word
picture</u>; both can become straightforward descriptions when they are meant
only as comparisons. Interpretation must get behind words and statements and work
in terms of the nature of the thing or situation itself. Nature of the case
overcomes dependence on words by accessing experience. Language refers only to
part of the referent; language puts the reality in front of hearers minds. When
they think in terms of the whole referent, they are less likely to make
erroneous inferences. Correct understanding depends on experience to provide
information about the referent aside from the statement. Nature of the case contrasts
with <u>illustrations</u> (<i>vs.</i> examples or cases), <u>analogical
reasoning</u>, and <u>formal logic</u>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   Nature of the case
approximates <u>intuitive thought</u> <i>vs.</i> <u>discursive reasoning</u>. Distinguishing
apples and oranges does not reason to a conclusion; it recognizes intuitively the
difference between them.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   Nature of the case is
illustrated by interpersonal experience. Horizontal experience with other
persons helps understanding vertical relationship to God. Vertical relationship
a personal God motivates proper horizontal relationships. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   With nature of the case comes
a warning for interpretation and reasoning in the scriptures. If our perception
of the reality is off, <u>we</u> will be adding to biblical content those assumptions
that skew the resulting combination. Besides, we tentatively assume the
correctness of a <u>writers</u> idea as a whole beyond what the writer
actually says.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   Words <i>vs.</i> referents is
comparable to symbols <i>vs.</i> sounds. Homophones have the same sound with
different meaning: </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>as <i>bow</i>
and <i>beau</i> look different but refer to the same sound so also different
words can refer to the same thing. The <i>g</i> in <i>distinguish</i>
correlates with the <i>c</i> in <i>distin<u>c</u>tion</i>; even though the two
letters look nothing alike, the difference is that the first is voiced and the
second is not.</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> Getting behind the symbols
allows a person to see an oral connection behind those words that would not
exist visually on paper. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   Working from first principles is
better than working from statements. Working from words is what most people are
doing when people stress logic. They are taking advantage of the wording of a
text instead of listening to the meaning of the context. The problem with
statements is that words are relatively imprecise. Reality thinking gets behind
the imprecision of words and deals with the implications of the nature of the
thing itself. Of course, mental inference can err here too because the mind may
not adequately know the real nature of the object of consideration, but
language compounds the problem by adding the imprecision of words to the lack
of awareness of the reality.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   The importance of the nature
of the case can be illustrated by examples of <u>equivocation</u>treating
unlike things as they were alike. </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
color:#7030A0'>Some have equated unlike things in arguing that the commandment
against eating blood prohibits blood transfusions. They have either misconstrued
the meaning of the word <i>eat</i> or misgeneralized it from the commandment to
a foreign application (what it meant to what it means). Eating blood is not
like transfusion, because eating of blood would have been <u>animal</u> blood;
many times it would have been involved in pagan <u>worship</u> rites.
Worshipers might drink the blood of a slain bull as a way of ingesting the
power of the animal. Transfusions are not for revelry. The Hebrew word for
eat could not include transfusions, because such a practice did not exist in
biblical times. Eating and transfusions have a different <u>psychology</u> in
that eating blood may contribute to barbarism. Finally, transfusions are for <u>saving
life</u>, which is not the reason for eating blood.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   To think properly on any
subject, an interpreter has to have a correct <u>model</u> of the item. Model
contrasts with analogy because the point is to think about the whole reality, not
just the part highlighted by a statement. We cannot understand one kind of
reality adequately by applying to it the characteristics of another reality. A
person does not understand <u>conditionality</u> by trying to think of it as <u>causality</u>
(as used in everyday speaking). Conditionality moves only in the realm of
interpersonal relationships, where attitude (as well as sheer act), unquantifiability,
will, and emotion, apply. Conditionality does not have the characteristics of
logical sequence, natural necessity, or magical causality; nor is it like <u>antinomianism</u>
or <u>recognition</u>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   What we are calling nature of
the case Jesus referred to as righteous judgment (judging rightly; John <b>7</b>:24)
rather than superficially. The Pharisees should not judge by appearance or
after the flesh (John <b>8</b>:15; 1 Samuel <b>2</b>:3; 1<b>6</b>:7; 1 Kings <b>8</b>:39;
1 Chronicles <b>28</b>:9). Judgments are shallow when based on tangible elements
without considering motive and intentspirit. True judgment envisions the
whole, real picture.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   Profitable exegesis gets
beyond <u>biblical positivism</u>; that is, it gets beyond affirming
truthfulness and authority of a text even if a person does not know what it
means. Verbal positivism has no practical value because it is contentless.
Understanding requires (a) getting to the referents of words and (b) seeing how
the parts of the whole interconnect. Biblical interpretation seeks
understanding, which requires proper perception of the relationship of ideas,
not just atomized facts in unrelated texts affirmed in theory.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>One concept of unity from a doctrinal standpoint is based
on this notion of biblical positivism. Under this approach people affirm the
claims of scripture and say that scripture is true theoretically in regard to
whatever it means. Anything that speaks of trying to understand the ideas
themselves gets labeled speculation. Christians, however, must believe the
truth and mean the truth itself insofar as the expression of it is clear. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   Biblical positivism can mean
something healthy if it indicates a persons accepting points of revelation
that do not derive deductively from systematic considerations. The idea here
links up with one value of inerrancy. Regarding <u>commandments</u>, what does
not arise from the nature of the case must arise from authoritative
pronouncement through positive commandment. In this case, positive means not
necessarily implied by some more basic factor.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>   <u>Nature of the case is the
aspect of harmony</u> that deals with the <u>reality</u> under view, rather
than the <u>words</u> used. It embraces consistency. In given situations,
nature of the case combines with other aspects of the law of harmony and with
the law of negation. Pauls intent of meaning in husband of one wife, for
example, is clear from the word blameless in the <u>near context</u> of the
Titus <b>1</b>before and after the phrase at issue. It establishes the frame
of reference as a moral concern. <u>Distant context</u> indicates that whether
a person is married lies outside the moral frame of reference. From the nature
of the case, then, the interpreter eliminates the necessity of marriageand
other amoral considerationsfrom the scope of the apostles intent in this
qualification.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The most important <u>applications
of the nature of the case</u> come in connection with the items below: <u>inference</u>
from what is actually said and <u>application</u> to situations not originally
envisioned.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (a) Understanding comparisons,
as in metaphors, similes, type-antitypes, and parables; nature of the case
helps eliminate allegorizing comparisons.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (b) Consider an expression
figurative or literal; knowing the nature of the case separates fact from
figure.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (c) Reasoning in the
scripture; the interpreter decides whether different statements in the Bible
relate to each other</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (d) Selecting between
alternative meanings of a text</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (e) Theological
interpretation, which attempts to generalize specifics addressed in scripture
and to deal with the crucial issues of modern life through principles extracted
from those biblical specifics (what it meant <i>vs.</i> what it means). The
nature of the case applies to inferences made from statements said.
Successfully working this system avoids transposing first-century cultural
expression of the gospel into the twenty-first century practice (eating with
sinners) and culturalizing the heathen instead of evangelizing them.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  (f) The significance to be attached
to silence</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>Did you ever try to wear out a mirror?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   **In Matthew <b>20</b>:28
(= Mark <b>10</b>:45) the word ransom must be taken figuratively by the
nature of the case, because Christs giving his life did not pay anyone.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   **In The Parable
of the Prodigal Son (Luke <b>15</b>:11-32), the prodigal was a son while he was
living riotously in the foreign country, but he was not a spiritual son. There
is a relevant difference between physical and interpersonal sonship.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   **Acts <b>20</b>:7
uses the phrase, <i>The first day of the week. </i><u>The</u> with a date
does not mean every so as to argue for weekly communion. The definite article
with a date amounts to every only if on other grounds we know the author is
talking about a recurring date. In other words, it depends on the situation. The
women came to Jesus tomb on <i>the first day of the week</i> (Luke<b> 24</b>:1).
That was not a recurrent event.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   **Ephesians <b>2</b>:1
uses the expression <i>dead in trespasses and sins.</i> Some have argued on
this basis that a sinner is as insensible to spiritual matters as a corpse is
to its physical surroundings. Paul means insensitive to spiritual matters and
therefore dead.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   **Some have used
Ephesians <b>5</b>:18 to say that a person under the influence of the Holy
Spirit cannot control himself any more than a person drunk with wine can
control himself. Paul has contrast in mind, not comparison as 1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:32
shows.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   **A
long-standing analogy used to support evolutionary philosophy has been that one
monkey given enough time could sit at a typewriter and eventually produce the
works of Shakespeare in the correct order. The problem is that the illustration
is not like what it illustrates: entropy (the tendency in nature toward
disorganization, deterioration, unavailability of energy) is left out of the
picture. So to speak, entropy comes along and removes some of the letters from
the manuscript. Besides, the illustration pictures straight-line series rather
than the interdependence of parts in living organisms. Interdependent parts
cannot originate in sequence.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  1. The concept of necessity,
possibility/impossibility</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Necessity may apply to different
<u>degrees</u>, different <u>kinds</u>, and different <u>subjects</u>. As to
kinds, necessity can be interpersonal, legal, natural, logical, or situational.
As to subjects, necessity relates to purpose; so the necessity may differ from
purpose to purpose. The kind and degree of necessity arises from the nature of
the case. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> There is also a difference
between <u>necessary</u> and <u>sufficient</u>. Some factor may be crucial to
an effect but other factors may be crucial as well. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  A number of words and phrases
relate to necessity: must needs do such and such, it is necessary, it
needs to be, it must, it behooves, it is appropriate. Relevant Greek
terms are </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>(<i>dei</i>),
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>(<i>anangk</i>),
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>(<i>anangkaz</i>),
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> (<i>anangkaion</i>), </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'> (<i>is
possible/impossible exestin</i>). The kind and degree of necessity and
impossibility depends on the nature of the situation and the kind of thing the
author is talking about. There can be legal necessity, natural necessity,
interpersonal necessity, logical necessity, practical necessity, or consequent
necessity coming from a previous consideration that is itself variable
(contingent). As to <u>kinds and degrees of necessity</u>, <i>It was necessary
for him to do this</i> is light enough to mean <i>He needed to do this</i>
or <i>It is appropriate for him to do this.</i> </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>(<i>dei</i>) covers even practical necessity, which
allows for other possibilities for dealing with a practical problem. Necessity,
then, includes appropriateness and moral obligation in addition to inherent
necessity. The word </span><i><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> is broad enough for something akin to what will
happen.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>(<i>dei</i>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**Many unfortunate events had to happen, and the gospel
had to be preached throughout the Mediterranean world before the end of the age
would come (Matthew<b> 24</b>:6 = Luke <b>21</b>:9; Mark <b>13</b>:7, 10).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Matthew <b>26</b>:51-53:
Jesus had to die to fulfill scripture (practical necessity; given prophecy, he
had to die); yet <b>26</b>:54 says that he could have called twelve legions of
angels (hence, not inherent necessity). He had to die given Gods intention to
call on Christs disciples to die; otherwise, his disciples would have been
above their Lord. A leader does not call on his followers to do what he is not
willing to do (Matthew <b>10</b>:38; <b>16</b>:24 = Mark 8:34 = Luke <b>9</b>:23;
Luke <b>14</b>:27; Romans <b>8</b>:29, 31-39). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **In Luke <b>13</b>:16
Jesus told the ruler of the synagogue that it was necessary for this daughter
of Abraham to be released from the demon that had bowed her over for eighteen
years. It was <u>appropriate</u> that she be releasedgiven reston the Sabbath.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The father of
the prodigal son told the older brother that it was necessary for them to make
merry (Luke<b> 15</b>:32).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Jesus told
Zacchaeus that he needed to stay in his house that night (Luke <b>19</b>:5). Jesus
could have spent the night in any number of other places.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **When Jesus
left Judaea to go to Galilee, John <b>4</b>:4 says, <i>And he had to go
through Samaria.</i> He had to go through Samaria if he went due north, but
he did not have to go north. He could have taken the typical route eastward
down across the Jordan, up the river on the other side, and back across just
south of the Sea of Galilee. Necessity here exists only as a function of a
prior consideration.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **According to
Acts <b>5</b>:29 the apostles had to obey God rather man, yet in fact most
people do not do that. They had to obey God to be consistent with their
convictions.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The Lord tells
Ananias that Paul had to suffer many things for Christs sake (Acts<b> 9</b>:16;
<b>10</b>:6).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **According to
Acts<b> 17</b>:3 in Thessalonica Paul reasoned that it was necessary for the
Messiah to suffer. His point may not argue for an inherent necessity of
substitutionary suffering but for a necessity based on the prediction. In light
of the predictions that he would suffer, it was a necessary mark of Messiah
that he suffer (cp. Matthew <b>15</b>:21; <b>26</b>:54; Mark <b>8</b>:31; Luke <b>9</b>:22;
<b>17</b>:25;<b> 22</b>:37; <b>24</b>:7, 26, 44, 46; John <b>3</b>:16; <b>12</b>:34;
Acts <b>17</b>:3</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **People have to
help the weak (Acts <b>20</b>:35) necessary in the sense of moral obligation
and basic decency.</span></p>
