<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **It was
necessary for the sailors to have listened to Paul on the voyage to Rome, but
they did not listen (Acts <b>27</b>:21).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Paul had to be
brought before Caesar (Acts<b> 27</b>:24; cp. <b>25</b>:10).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The laborer
must be the first partaker (2 Timothy <b>2</b>:6).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **It is
necessary for the servant of the Lord not to quarrel (2 Timothy <b>2</b>:24).
The idea seems to be appropriate more than necessary.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **A higher
degree of necessity is evident in the circumstance described by the Hebrew writer
(<b>11</b>:6) when he says that <i>without faith it is impossible to please
God, because he that comes to God must believe that he exists and that he is a
rewarder of them that diligently seek him.</i> A person will not be coming to
God unless he believes that he exists.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**Several passages are translated ought or should: Matthew
1<b>8</b>:33; <b>25</b>:27; Mark <b>13</b>:14; Romans <b>8</b>:26;<b> 12</b>:3;
1 Corinthians<b> 8</b>:2; 2 Corinthians <b>2</b>:3; Ephesians <b>6</b>:20 =
Colossians<b> 4</b>:4; <b>4</b>:6; 1 Thessalonians <b>4</b>:1; 2 Thessalonians<b>
3</b>:7; 1 Timothy<b> 3</b>:15; <b>5</b>:13; Titus <b>1</b>:11b; Hebrews <b>2</b>:1;
2 Peter<b> 3</b>:1</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>anank</i><u>)</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **<i>Offenses
must come </i>(Matthew<b> 18</b>:7), meaning <i>offences are going to come.
Count on it.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **One guest
invited to a banquet would not come because he had to go see some land he had
bought (Luke 1<b>4</b>:18).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Pilate had
to release a political prisoner at the Passover feast, a custom he himself had
originated to placate the hostility of the Jews against his rule (Luke <b>23</b>:17).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **According to 1
Corinthians <b>9</b>:16, Paul had necessity laid on him to preach the gospelsomething
that was actually a sense of moral obligation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **In Jude 3 he
says that he <u>needed</u> to write.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>anangkaion</i><u>)</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **According to
Acts <b>13</b>:46, it was necessary to preach the gospel to the Jews before
preaching it to the Gentiles. The point was that for the sake of appropriateness
or practical advantage, it was best to do it that way. God had already prepared
them to hear it.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The more
feeble parts of the body are necessary (1 Corinthians <b>12</b>:22).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  2. The concept of inability
(cannot/is-not-able, </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'></span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt'>[<i>dynamai</i>]
)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Inability has a number of
kinds and degrees. Besides (a) inherent inability it can mean (b) not being
allowed (may not), (c) circumstantial inability, (d) given certain assumed
conditions. The last two entries are matters of consistency. Cannot, then, may
mean cannot naturally, morally, legally, circumstantially, cannot without much
difficulty, cannot without certain undesirable consequences (<i>I cannot
rise, </i>that is, without embarrassment?; Genesis<b> 31</b>:35), cannot in
the sense that I do not want to, or cannot in the sense that I do not know
how.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**Judges<b> 12</b>:6 says that the Ephraimites could not
say <i>Shibboleth</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>dynamai</i>) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Matthew 2<b>6</b>:42
records Jesus as saying, <i>If this cup </i>[crucifixion] <i>is not able to
pass from me . . .</i>; but he told Peter later (<b>26</b>:53) that he could call
twelve legions of angels. The cup was not able to pass from him in the sense
that it could not and scripture yet be fulfilled.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Mark <b>1</b>:45
says that Jesus was not able any longer to enter into the cities </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> in Galilee.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Mark <b>2</b>:19<span
style='position:relative;top:-3.0pt'>2</span>says that the sons of the bride
chamber cannot fast as long as the bridegroom is with them (cp. Matthew <b>9</b>:15).
Luke<b> 6</b>:39 goes ahead to say that you cannot make them fast in such circumstances.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **At the height
of Jesus popularity, people were pressing in around him so hard that he and
his disciples could not even eat (Mark <b>3</b>:20).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Mark <b>6</b>:5
says Jesus could not do any mighty works in Nazareth because of the peoples
unbelief; yet he replaced the ear of Malchus in the Garden of Gethsemane when
Peter cut it off.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **In Tyre and
Sidon Jesus was not able to be hid (Mark<b> 7</b>:24), but he was able to hide
himself on more than one occasion in the crowds in Jerusalem.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Mark <b>9</b>:39
says that someone who does a mighty work in Jesus name cannot quickly speak
evil of him. This is a behavioral observation on the psychological character of
persons.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The man of the
house tells the neighbor knocking at his door that he cannot get up to get him
any bread (Luke<b> 11</b>:7); yet Jesus adds that because of their friendship
the man will get up and get bread for his friend (<b>11</b>:8). In this case,
cannot equals really does not want to.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The man who
had gotten married could not come to the feast because he had married a wife
(Luke <b>14</b>:20; cp. Deuteronomy<b> 24</b>:5; 1 Corinthians <b>7</b>:33).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **People cannot
be Jesus disciples unless they hate their family and their own life, take up
a cross, and gives up everything they owns (Luke <b>11</b>:14, 26-27, 33).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The landowner
told the unjust steward that he could not be steward any longer (Luke <b>16</b>:2);
that is, he would not be allowed to. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Jesus said
that he could do nothing of himself (John <b>5</b>:30), meaning obviously that
he could do nothing on his own and be son.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Supposedly the
world was not able to hate Jesus disciples (John <b>7</b>:7) even though most
of them were martyred.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **John <b>14</b>:17<i>:
. . . whom</i> [the Spirit] <i>the world cannot receive <u>because it </u></i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  <i><u>cannot
see him</u>. . . .</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **<i>Without/apart-from
me you cannot do anything </i>(John <b>15</b>:5). <i>Cannot</i> in this case may
be taken circumstantially rather than ability-wise. Nothing of lasting value is
done aside from Christian orientation. <i>Cannot</i> could be in a relative
sense here along with <i>anything</i> in a relative sense as well.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Jesus did not
tell his disciples everything up front because they were not able to bear them
at the time (John<b> 16</b>:12; cp. Mark <b>4</b>:33; 1 Corinthians<b> 3</b>:1).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The Sanhedrin members
they could not deny the apostles healing of the lame man at Gate Beautiful
(Acts <b>4</b>:16).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **In Acts <b>4</b>:20
Peter tells the rulers of Israel that he and the other apostles could not help
speaking what they had seen and heard.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Peter asked
whether anyone could forbid water for baptizing the household of Cornelius
(Acts <b>10</b>:47).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **In Acts <b>17</b>:19
the Areopagites ask whether they could know what Paul was teachinganother case
of ability in the sense of permission.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **In Caesarea
Paul claims that no one could turn him over to the Jews for trial (Acts <b>25</b>:11),
obviously meaning that they could not do so without breaking Roman law
regarding the privileges of Roman citizenship.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Paul could not
do anything against the truth (2 Corinthians <b>13</b>:8).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Some good
works cannot be hid (1 Timothy<b> 5</b>:25).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **The saints of
Ephesus were not able to bear evil men (Revelation <b>2</b>:2). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>   </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>ischy</i><u>)</u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **In Luke <b>16</b>:3
the unjust steward says he is not able to dig.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span lang=FR
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>/</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
color:#7030A0'> </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'></span><span
lang=FR style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> (<i>exestin/ouk exestin</i><u>)</u>
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
lang=FR style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>Hebrews <b>10</b>:4: <i>The blood of
bulls and goats cannot take away sin</i>; yet to the Old Testament people God
clearly said that the blood of bulls and goats <u>could</u> take away sin. The
difference lies in the sense and circumstance of usageinherent necessity <i>vs.</i>
conditional necessity.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> Matthew<b> 19</b>:11<i>:
Not all men are able to receive this saying</i> [that it is better not </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> to get married].<i></i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  3. The role of silence</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The role of silence depends on
convention, the nature of the case, and literary</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> genre.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  Silence may or may not be
significant silence. It may be significant on the basis of (a) the <u>nature of
the case</u>. In some situations, one option necessarily eliminates all
parallel possibilities; in others it may not. Silence may create presumption of
significance if there is (b) <u>strong relevance to the topic in the context</u>.
The limitation here is that not all things apparently relevant need be
addressed or cited in a presentation. If the body of literature is large
enough, the significance of the silence may be enhanced. Usually, however, in
matters approached under this second form of significant silence, silence
confirms, not proves. Silence can be meaningful as shown, for example, by what
is called a zero ending on words.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  To evaluate appeals to
silence, the reader needs to ask whether one would expect scriptureor <u>this</u>
scriptureto speak on the topic. Does it lie right in the path of what certain
contexts address?</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  The silence of scripture has
been brought to bear on a number of issues including: </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> </span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>**the normativeness of New Testament church polity
(Baptists, Christian </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  church).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **the
prohibition of instrumental music in worship </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **the
prohibition of church buildings, choirs, Sunday schools, parachurch </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  agencies in
general.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **not making
public appeals for financial support </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> The we
passages in the Book of Acts show when the author was present with Paul. The
absence of we in other places does not necessarily show that Luke was absent.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> All New
Testament books were written before the fall of Jerusalem because none of them
mention this most significant event in the history of Gods dealing with Israel.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> Sexual
unfaithfulness is the only grounds for divorce because no others are </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  mentioned.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> the belief that
we are under all the Old Testament laws except the ones that </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'>  have been
specifically withdrawn</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> the idea that
what is not prohibited is okay</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> the idea that
what is not commanded does not have to be done</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **What does the
absence of a sign reading no right turn on red mean? The silence may mean
the driver may turn right or it may mean he cannot turn right. (a) If the
general principle in the traffic regulations permits right turns on red when
the way is clear, the absence means the driver may turn. (b) If traffic law
prohibits as a general principle passing into an intersection during a red
light, the silence reinforces the prohibition against the right turn. In the
first situation, it takes a special sign to prohibit the turn; in the second it
takes a special sign to permit the turn. The role of silence here ends up being
determined by convention, context, and the nature of the case. (c) Silence as
meaningful silence is illustrated by zero endings in word inflection.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **whether there
is a positive commandment that reserves a certain area for authorized behavior
only (Hebrews <b>7</b>:14 re worship, <i>e.g.</i>). Nature of the case might
not require authorization for approval, but God does have the authority to specify
behaviors in such areas. The point is whether he does so.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> **Pro-choice
activists argue that since the New Testament does not include abortion in its
lists of proscribed behaviors, the matter is up to the mother as to what she
wants to do. The weakness of the argument on this topic is that the silence may
be accounted for on other grounds besides approval. We could even argue that
silence regarding pro-abortion means it was not acceptable. It may not have
come up as a vice to be prohibited because all Christian readers in the first
century were agreed on it. Perhaps it was assumed under prohibitions against
murder. Maybe it was not a procedure that a common person even had access to.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> If basketball
players are warming up before a game, the coach does not tell one of them to
quit hitting warm-up shots because they will use them up before the game
begins. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>For application of the nature of the case as an
argument against the literalness of substitution imagery in atonement theory,
see <i>What the Bible Says About Salvation</i>, pp. 54-69, and related essays
elsewhere in our internet materials.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;color:#7030A0'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>  4. Double verb for composite idea (hendiadys)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> There are three possibilities when
two verbs appear: (1) composite idea (part-to-whole), (2) sequential ideas, or (3)
parallel ideas.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> <i>See God and live</i> may
mean see God while alive rather than seeing God would kill a person.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> Acts <b>10</b>:46: <i>spoke
in languages and glorified God</i> probably means glorifying God by the
speaking in languages rather than two actions (cp. Acts <b>19</b>:6).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 1 Timothy <b>2</b>:12: <i>teach
or exercise authority over a man</i> likely means teach authoritatively (hendiadys)
rather than teach as one act and exercise authority as another.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:-.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.25in;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-align:justify;line-height:12.0pt'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt'> 
</span><span style='font-size:11.0pt'>christir.org</span></p>
</div>
